--- Commit Message ---
LU-19054 utils: New max client connection limit.

This introduces the client_limit parameter that
allow a maximum number of client connections to be set.

client_limit can be set to limit the allowed number of
client-server connections. By default set to -1 for unlimited
connections.

This only affects client to server connections. Server to server
connections are unaffected.

Signed-off-by: Max Dilger <mdilger@whamcloud.com>
Change-Id: Ibef99a9bd1f889abdfeb97942600b66e9a9be123

## Summary

**Fix Applied:** Removed the unused variable `is_server` from the `nm_member_del()` function in `lustre/ptlrpc/nodemap_member.c`.

**Rationale:** 
The patch introduced a local variable `bool is_server;` on line 32 of the function, but this variable was never assigned or used anywhere in the function. The code directly calls `is_server_connection(&exp->exp_connect_data)` inline within the conditional statement on line 49, making the variable declaration unnecessary. 

Since the build is configured with `-Werror` (treat warnings as errors) and the compiler detected this unused variable with the `-Wunused-variable` warning, the compilation failed. The fix simply removes the unused variable declaration, allowing the code to compile successfully while maintaining the same functionality.

Patch Set 26:

I attempted to fix the build errors present in this patch and succeeded. Yay! Now, keep in mind I barely have any idea what I am doing, so please doublecheck the changes I made to make sure they make sense.

This service is only provided in hopes to be useful and reduce latency from push to getting actual results in the face of trivial code errors

Here's summary of my changes:
## Fix Explanation

**The Problem:**
The patch introduced a compile error in the `target_handle_disconnect` function at line 1774 of `lustre/ldlm/ldlm_lib.c`. The variable `exp` was incorrectly declared as `int` instead of `struct obd_export *`:

```c
int exp = req->rq_export;  // WRONG - req->rq_export is a pointer, not an int
```

This caused multiple compilation errors:
1. **Type mismatch on initialization**: Assigning a pointer to an int variable
2. **Invalid function arguments**: Passing an int where pointer functions expected `struct obd_export *`
3. **Invalid pointer dereference**: Using `->` operator on an int variable

**The Fix:**
Changed line 1774 from:
```c
int exp = req->rq_export;
```

to:
```c
struct obd_export *exp = req->rq_export;
```

**Rationale:**
- `req->rq_export` is a pointer to `struct obd_export`, not an integer
- The variable `exp` is used throughout the function with pointer operations (`->` operator) and passed to functions expecting `struct obd_export *`
- This was clearly a typo in the patch where the author intended to create a local pointer variable for convenience but accidentally declared it with the wrong type
- The fix aligns with how the code was used in the rest of the function (lines 1790, 1795, 1801-1802)
